Power Concurrent with Act: Objection to Obligation
Fourth objection: power simultaneous with act voids obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the view that power is simultaneous with the act leads to the impossibility of religious obligation (taklif).

Core Idea
If power is only at the act, obligation before it is impossible.

This passage presents a logical objection against the Ash‘ari position that power (qudra) is simultaneous with the act. If power does not precede the act, then at the moment of command the person has no power, making obligation meaningless. Moreover, disobedience becomes logically impossible. This argument is used to show that power must precede the act if obligation is to be coherent.

Guided Path
1
Read the objection statement
Begin by reading the Arabic text and its translation. Notice the conditional structure: 'if power is with the act, then...'.
The objection is a reductio ad absurdum.
2
Identify the two consequences
The argument draws two consequences: (1) the disbeliever is not obligated to faith, and (2) disobedience from anyone is inconceivable. Locate these in the passage.
The first consequence is explicit; the second is derived from the reasoning.
3
Understand the logic behind each
For the first: at the time of command, the disbeliever has no power over faith (since power is only at the act). For the second: if the act is done, there is no disobedience; if not done, there is no power to do it – so disobedience cannot occur.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
The passage concludes that obligation becomes impossible. Reflect on how this argument supports the view that power must precede the act.
This is a classic kalam argument used in debates on qadar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الوجه (الرابع:) إن كانت القدرة على الفعل معه لا قبله ( يلزم أن لا يكون الكافر) في زمان كفره ( مكلفاً بالإيمان لأنه غير مقدور له في تلك الحالة المتقدمة عليه، بل نقول يلزم أن لا يتصور عصيان من أحد إذ مع الفعل لا عصيان وبدونه لا قدرة فلا تكليف فلا
The fourth aspect: If power over the act is with it, not before it, then it would follow that the disbeliever, at the time of his disbelief, is not obligated to faith, because it is not within his power in that state preceding it. Rather we say: it would follow that disobedience from anyone is inconceivable, for with the act there is no disobedience, and without it there is no power, so there is no obligation, so...
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage presents the fourth logical objection against the view that power is simultaneous with the act. If power only exists at the moment of the act, then before the act there is no power. Therefore, the disbeliever cannot be commanded to faith because at the time of command (before the act) he lacks power. Moreover, disobedience becomes impossible: if the act is done, there is no disobedience; if it is not done, there is no power. So obligation is void. This is a classic kalam argument used to show that power must precede the act to ground obligation.

Key Terms
قدرة
فعل
تكليف
كافر
إيمان
عصيان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that obligation only requires ability at the time of the act, so power could be simultaneous.
Correction: This argument shows that the command precedes the act, so ability must be present at the time of command; otherwise the command is meaningless.

Checkpoint
What does this argument conclude if power is with the act?
A) The disbeliever cannot be obligated to faith.
B) The disbeliever has power at the time of command.
C) Obligation is based on future power.
D) Power and act are simultaneous.

Key Takeaway
If power is only at the act, then command obligations become logically impossible, proving that power must precede the act.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever delayed fulfilling a religious obligation (like prayer or repentance) because you felt you lacked the ability at that moment? According to this argument, does that delay actually mean you are treating that command as non-obligatory? How does that compel you to change your approach?
?
If you truly held the belief that God gives you power only at the exact moment of action, would you still feel responsible for your future sins? How does this argument challenge any complacency you might have about sins you have not yet committed?
?
Consider one command of Allah that you find difficult to obey. When you think about that command, do you assume you will have the power when the time comes, or do you feel you lack the power now? This argument says that power must precede obligation—so where does that leave you? Are you willing to ask Allah for that power now, not later?

Divine Attributes
intermediate
5 min
The Problem of Temporal Power and the Essential Distinction
The author states the problem of temporal power preceding the act and gives the essential distinction as the first part of the answer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the problem of temporal power preceding the act arises and how the Ash'ari school resolves it by distinguishing the essence of eternal power from temporal power.

Core Idea
Eternal power and temporal power differ in essence, so their precedence rules differ.

This lesson introduces a key problem in kalam: if temporal power exists before the act, what prevents it from causing the act earlier? The author first presents the difficulty and then offers the foundational solution: eternal and temporal power are essentially different, so the permissibility of one does not transfer to the other.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem
Read the first part of the passage which defines temporal power and its connection to the act. Notice the objection raised.
2
Understand the essential distinction
The author states that eternal power differs in essence from temporal power. Reflect on why this distinction resolves the initial problem.
Temporal power cannot remain, so it cannot precede the act indefinitely.
3
Apply the principle
Consider how this reasoning prevents the conclusion that temporal power could also precede the act.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
النوع الرابع - المقصد الخامس : القدرة الحادثة وتعلقها بالفعل. تثبت القدرة قبل الفعل مع تعلقها به في الجملة (وأيضا) إن امتنع تعلق القدرة بالفعل في الأزل لامتناع كون الفعل أزلياً (فالتعلق) أي تعلقها بالفعل (قبله بزمان) متناه لا يمتنع فيرد الاشكال بحسبه أي بحسب هذا التعلق، إذ حينئذ تكون القدرة موجودة قبل الفعل ومتعلقة به أيضاً قبله بزمان محدود كان الفعل فيه ممكناً، فالصواب في الجواب أن يقال القدرة القديمة الباقية مخالفة في الماهية للقدرة الحادثة التي لا يجوز بقاؤها عندنا. فلا يلزم من جواز تقدمها على الفعل جواز تقدم الحادثة عليه، ثم إن القدرة القديمة متعلقة في الأزل بالفعل تعلقاً معنوياً لا يترتب عليه وجود الفعل ولها تعلق آخر به حال حدوثه تعلقاً حادثاً موجباً، لوجوده فلا يلزم من قدمها مع تعلقها المعنوي قدم آثارها فاندفع الاشكال بحذافيره.
The fourth type - fifth objective: The temporal power and its connection to the act. Power is established before the act with its connection to it in general. (And also) if the connection of power to the act in pre-eternity is impossible because the act cannot be pre-eternal, (the connection) i.e., its connection to the act (before it by a time) finite is not impossible; so the problem arises with respect to it, i.e., with respect to this connection, because then power exists before the act and is also connected to it before it by a limited time in which the act was possible. The correct answer is to say: The eternal, remaining power is different in essence from the temporal power which, according to us, cannot remain. So the permissibility of its precedence over the act does not imply the permissibility of the temporal (power) preceding it. Then the eternal power is connected in pre-eternity to the act with a conceptual connection (ta'alluq ma'nawī) that does not entail the existence of the act, and it has another connection to it at the time of its occurrence, a temporal connection (ta'alluq ḥādith) that necessitates its existence. So its eternalness along with its conceptual connection does not entail the eternalness of its effects. Thus the problem is repelled entirely.
Source pages p. 102

Commentary
This passage defines the problem of the relation of temporal power to the act and provides the correct answer according to the Ash'ari school. It begins by stating that temporal power is generally established before the act, but a problem arises when considering a finite time before the act. The correct answer is that the eternal divine power (al-qudra al-qadīma al-bāqiya) is different in essence (mukhālifa fī al-māhiyya) from temporal power (al-qudra al-ḥāditha), which cannot persist. Therefore, the fact that eternal power can precede the act does not imply that temporal power can also precede it. The author then explains that eternal power has two types of connection to the act: a conceptual connection (ta'alluq ma'nawī) in pre-eternity that does not cause the act's existence, and a temporal connection (ta'alluq ḥādith) at the time of the act that necessitates its existence. Thus, the eternal power's pre-existence does not entail the pre-existence of its effects, resolving the problem entirely.

Key Terms
القدرة الحادثة
القدرة القديمة
الماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that if eternal power can precede the act, then temporal power can also precede it.
Correction: The author clarifies that the two types of power differ in essence, so the rule for one does not apply to the other.

Checkpoint
According to the author, why does the permissibility of eternal power's precedence not imply the permissibility of temporal power's precedence?
A) Because temporal power does not exist.
B) Because they differ in essence.
C) Because eternal power is not truly power.
D) Because the act is eternal.

Key Takeaway
The essential difference between eternal and temporal power prevents transferring precedence from one to the other.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have just learned that God's power is fundamentally different in essence from any power you experience. How does this correct any assumptions you have made about how God 'must' operate—especially when you have doubted His ability to fulfill His promises?
?
Consider a time you were impatient, expecting something to happen immediately because 'power' was present. How does the distinction between remaining and non-remaining power challenge you to trust God's timing differently?
?
If God's power is eternal and remains, while your power fades, what does that demand of your reliance on Him versus your own abilities? Be specific: what area of your life do you need to surrender because your power cannot sustain it?
